That should be fine, just redundant.

Another edge case: what if the value is set programmatically while the popover is open? The `_needsHighlightAfterRender` flag would not be set, so no scroll/highlight would happen. But that's probably the correct behavior - we don't want to hijack the user's scrolling if they've already navigated in the list.

What about the first render? If a select has an initial value, does it need to scroll on first open? Yes - when the user first opens the select, `OpenMenu` is called, `_needsHighlightAfterRender` is set, and after the render the highlight and scroll happen. This is the exact scenario described in the PR.

Let me also consider: the `HighlightItemForValueAsync` method uses `_context.TryGetItemByValue`. But wait, at `OnAfterRenderAsync` time, are items registered? Let me trace through:

1. `OpenMenu()` sets `_openState.Value = true` and calls `StateHasChanged()`
2. Blazor renders the component. The popover opens and `ChildContent` (which includes `MudSelectItem` components) renders.
3. During rendering, `MudSelectItem.OnMudSelectChanged` is called (because the `CascadingValue` for `IMudSelect` provides the context). This registers the item in the context.
4. After all rendering is complete, `OnAfterRenderAsync` is called. At this point, items ARE registered.

But wait - there's a subtlety. The `CascadingValue` passes `this` (the MudSelect) to items. But `CascadingValue` values are propagated during rendering. The question is: does `OnMudSelectChanged` get called during the same render cycle? Let me check `MudSelectItem.cs`:

The `OnMudSelectChanged` is a parameter change handler registered in the constructor:
```csharp
registerScope.RegisterParameter<IMudSelect?>(nameof(IMudSelect))
    .WithParameter(() => IMudSelect)
    .WithChangeHandler(OnMudSelectChanged);
```

In MudBlazor's parameter state system, the change handler is called during `SetParametersAsync` which happens before `OnAfterRenderAsync`. So yes, items will be registered by the time `OnAfterRenderAsync` runs.

Let me double-check by looking at how `OnMudSelectChanged` works more carefully. The `IMudSelect` cascading parameter is set during rendering. But when does the change handler fire? Looking at `MudComponentBase` and the parameter state system, change handlers are invoked during `OnParametersSetAsync` which happens as part of the component lifecycle before rendering.

Actually, wait. Let me look at the MudSelectItem's `OnMudSelectChanged` again:

```csharp
private void OnMudSelectChanged(ParameterChangedEventArgs<IMudSelect?> args)
{
    if (args.LastValue?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> oldContext)
    {
        _selectionSubscription?.Dispose();
        _selectionSubscription = null;
        oldContext.UnregisterItem(this);
    }

    if (args.Value?.SelectContext is MudSelectContext<T> newContext)
    {
        _context = newContext;
        var isSelected = _context.RegisterItem(this);
        Selected = isSelected;
        _selectionSubscription = _context.SubscribeToSelectionChanges(OnSelectionChangedAsync);
    }
}
```

This is called when `IMudSelect` parameter changes. But for the initial render, the `IMudSelect` cascading parameter is set for the first time. In that case, `args.LastValue` would be null (no previous value) and `args.Value` would be the select. So it would register the item.

But when does this happen? In the Blazor lifecycle, cascading parameters are set during `SetParametersAsync`. The `OnMudSelectChanged` handler is called by the parameter state system. 

Let me check if there's a potential issue where items are rendered but their parameter change handlers haven't been called yet when `OnAfterRenderAsync` of the parent runs. The answer is: no. `OnAfterRenderAsync` on the parent runs after all child components have been rendered. And child components' `OnParametersSetAsync` (where parameter change handlers run) happens before their own render.

So the flow is:
1. Parent `OpenMenu()` → sets state, calls `StateHasChanged()`
2. Blazor calls `SetParametersAsync` on parent (if needed)
3. Blazor calls `OnParametersSetAsync` on parent
4. Blazor renders parent, which includes rendering child MudSelectItem components
5. For each child:
   - `SetParametersAsync` is called, which sets the `IMudSelect` cascading parameter
   - The parameter change handler `OnMudSelectChanged` fires, registering the item
   - The child renders
6. Parent's `OnAfterRenderAsync` is called → now items are registered!

Great, so my fix should work correctly.

But I want to also consider another edge case: what if there's a `MudSelectItem` with `HideContent=true`? In that case, the item is a "shadow item" and doesn't render in the dropdown. The `OnMudSelectChanged` handler would still fire and register it. But for scrolling purposes, we only care about visible items (those in `_items`, not `_shadowLookup`). The `TryGetItemByValue` method looks in `_valueLookup` which contains visible items. So this is correct.

Now let me also consider: what about when there are no items at all (or no non-disabled items)? Let me check:

For single-select:
- `HighlightItemForValueAsync(ReadValue)` calls `_context.TryGetItemByValue(value, out var item)` which may return false
- `HighlightItemAsync(null)` just sets `_activeItemId = null` and calls `StateHasChanged`
- Then `_context.TryGetItemByValue(ReadValue, out var item)` again - if false, we don't scroll
- This is fine

For multi-select:
- `Items.FirstOrDefault(x => !x.Disabled)` returns null if no items
- `HighlightItemAsync(null)` is fine
- `ScrollToItemAsync(null)` is fine (returns `ValueTask.CompletedTask`)

All edge cases seem handled.

        public async Task OpenMenuAsync()
        {
            if (MinCharacters > 0 && (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(ReadText) || ReadText.Length < MinCharacters))
            {
                Open = false;
                StateHasChanged();
                return;
            }

            _opening = true;

            var searchedItems = Array.Empty<T>();
            CancelToken();

            var wasFocused = _isFocused;
            var searchingWhileSelected = false;
            try
            {
                if (ProgressIndicatorInPopoverTemplate != null)
                {
                    // Open before searching if a progress indicator is defined.
                    Open = true;
                }

                // Search while selected if enabled and the Text is equivalent to the Value.
                searchingWhileSelected = !_isValueCoerced && !Strict && ReadValue != null && (ReadValue!.ToString() == ReadText || (ToStringFunc != null && ToStringFunc(ReadValue!) == ReadText));
                _cancellationTokenSrc ??= new CancellationTokenSource();
                var searchText = searchingWhileSelected ? string.Empty : ReadText;
                var searchTask = SearchFunc?.Invoke(searchText, _cancellationTokenSrc.Token);

                _currentSearchTask = searchTask;

                StateHasChanged();
                searchedItems = searchTask switch
                {
                    null => [],
                    _ => (await searchTask).ToArray()
                };
            }
            catch (TaskCanceledException)
            {
            }
            catch (OperationCanceledException)
            {
            }
            catch (Exception e)
            {

Good, Autocomplete doesn't override `OnAfterRenderAsync`, so my changes don't affect it.

Let me now look at whether there's also an issue with the `SelectFirstItem` method when the select is opened via keyboard (e.g., ArrowDown). When the user presses ArrowDown:

1. `HandleArrowDownAsync` is called
2. If not open, it calls `OpenMenu()` (which now sets `_needsHighlightAfterRender = true`)
3. After render, `OnAfterRenderAsync` highlights and scrolls to the selected item

But wait, `HandleArrowDownAsync` also calls `SelectNextItem()` after `OpenMenu()` if already open. If not open, it just calls `OpenMenu()` and returns. So the highlight/scroll will happen via `OnAfterRenderAsync`. That's correct.

Let me also check `HandleArrowUpAsync`:
- If `AltKey`, it closes the menu
- If not open, it calls `OpenMenu()` 
- If open, it calls `SelectPreviousItem()`

Same pattern, correct.

`HandleEnterAsync`:
- If not open, calls `OpenMenu()` and returns

Also correct.

Now let's also consider: what about when `OpenMenu()` is called and there are items but no selected value? In that case:
- Single-select: `HighlightItemForValueAsync(ReadValue)` where `ReadValue` is default/null. This calls `_context.TryGetItemByValue(null, out var item)` which may or may not find an item (depends on whether there's an item with null value). Either way, it's fine.
- Multi-select: highlights the first non-disabled item. Fine.
